Jamison Brereton

83 (437)
Parjanya
Atri Bhauma
10 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh 1, 5тАУ8, 10, jagat─л 2тАУ4, anuс╣гс╣нubh 9
Parjanya (тАЬThunderтАЭ) is the subject of only three hymns in the R╠еgveda. This lovely hymn, much translated, is reminiscent of the Marut hymns in this maс╣Зс╕Нala, though not ascribed to the same poet. (The Maruts are addressed here in vs. 6.) Vivid images of the power of the thunderstorm are mingled with expressions of thanks for the fructifying effects of the accompanying rains, depicted as sexual in nature. In the last verse the poet describes all the good Parjanya has done, but gently urges him to desist.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Parjanya

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬI address the mighty Parjanya who is present; praise him with these hymns; worship him with reverence, him who is the thunderer, the showerer, the bountiful, who impregnates the plural nts with rain.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Parjanya: is Indra, as the sender of rain; Nirukta 10.10 provides a number of etymologies: par, derived from tс╣Ыp, to satisfy (with a reversal of the final consonant), janya = a victor, jet─Б or genitive rator janayith, or impelleer prajayit─Б, of fluids, ras─Бn─Бm; un─Бdi derivation refers it to vс╣Ыс╣г, to rain (p substituted for v; r. becoming the guс╣Зa, ar; and s’ being changed to j; anya is the affix)

Jamison Brereton

Address the powerful one with these hymns. Praise Parjanya. With reverence seek to entice him here.
The constantly roaring bull of lively drops deposits his semen as embryo in the plants.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The verb dadh─Бti can be read with both r├йtaс╕е and g├бrbham, the latter in the idiom g├бrbham тИЪdh─Б тАШimpregnateтАЩ, found again in 7a.

Griffith

SING with these songs thy welcome to the Mighty, with adoration praise and call Parjanya.
The Bull, loud roaring, swift to send his bounty, lays in the plants the seed. for germination.

Macdonell

Invoke the mighty god with songs of welcome; Parjanya praise: with homage seek to win him. He, roaring like a bull, with streams that quicken, A seed to germinate in plants deposits.

Geldner

Rufe mit diesen Lobesworten den Starken an, preise Parjanya, bitte ihn unter Verbeugung her! Br├╝llend legt der rasch gew├дhrende Bulle seinen Samen als Keim in die Pflanzen.

Grassmann

Mit diesen Liedern rede an den starken, Pardschanja preise, lock ihn her in Ehrfurcht; Es br├╝llet laut der Stier, der tropfenreiche, der Samen giesst als Keim in die Gew├дchse.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬHe strikes down the trees, he destroys the r─Бkс╣гasas, he terrifies the whole world by his mighty weapon; even the innocent man flies from the sender of rain, when Parjanya, thundering, slays the wicked.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

He smashes apart the trees and also smashes the demons. All creation fears him who has the mighty weapon.
And (even) the blameless one shrinks from the one of bullish powers, when Parjanya, thundering, smashes those who do ill.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. quickly modulates from the physical to the moral, with Parjanya the scourge not only of the trees but of demons and evil-doers.

Griffith

He smites the trees apart, he slays the demons: all life fears him who wields the mighty weapon.
From him exceeding strong fices e’en the guiltless, when thundering Parjanya smites the wicked.

Macdonell

The trees he shatters and he smites the demon host: The whole world trembles at his mighty weapon’s stroke, The guiltless man himself flees from the potent god, When miscreants Parjanya with his thunder strikes.

Geldner

Er zerschl├дgt die B├дume und erschl├дgt die Unholde; die ganze Welt hat vor ihm Furcht, der die gro├Яe Waffe f├╝hrt. Auch der Schuldlose geht dem Bullenstarken aus dem Wege, wenn Parjanya donnernd die ├Ьbelt├дter erschl├дgt.

Grassmann

Er f├дll’t die B├дume, f├дll’t die Nachtgespenster auch; das Weltall bebt vor ihm, der grosse Waffen tr├дgt, Vor dem gewalt’gen fliehet auch, wer schuldlos ist, so oft Pardschanja donnernd Uebelth├дter schl├дgt.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAs a charioteer, urging his horses with his whip, brings into view the messenger (of war), so Parjanya, (driving the clouds before him), makes manifest the messengers of the rain; the roaring of the lion-(like cloud) proclaims from afar that Parjanya overspreads the sky with rainy clouds.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The messenger of war: the text has only d┼лt─Бn = bhaс╣н─Бn, warriors

Jamison Brereton

Like a charioteer lashing out at his horses with a whip, he reveals his rain-bearing messengers.
From afar the thunderings of the lion rise up, when Parjanya produces his rain-bearing cloud.

Jamison Brereton Notes

We might expect *rath─л╠Бr iva here, to the vс╣Ыk─л╠Б-stem rath─л╠Б-, but the ending -─л╠Б must belong instead to the -├нn-stem rath├нn-, which does have an independent existence. See Oldenberg ad loc. I take the whip in the simile to be lightning; both a whip and a lightning flash are slender, fast, unpredictable, and have a non-straight trajectory. The flash of lightning would also do the revealing in p─Бda b. Note also that thunder is covered in p─Бda c and rain in b and d, so lightning is whatтАЩs otherwise absent.

тАЬRain-bearing cloudтАЭ (varс╣гy├ас╣Г n├бbhaс╕е) in d seems like a quick and a bit halfhearted poetic repair of тАЬrain-bearing messengersтАЭ (d┼лt─Б╠Бn тАж varс╣гy─Б╠Аn) in b. The two p─Бdas hold the verb kс╣Ыс╣Зute constant.

Griffith

Like a car-driver whipping on his horses, he makes the messengers of rain spring forward.
Far off resounds the roaring of the lion, what time Parjanya fills the sky with rain-cloud.

Macdonell

Like charioteer his horses lashing with a whip, The god makes manifest his messengers of rain. From far away the roaring of the lion sounds, What time Parjanya veils the firmament with rain.

Geldner

Wie der Wagenfahrer mit der Peitsche auf die Rosse schlagend, l├д├Яt er seine Regenboten erscheinen. Von Ferne erheben sich die Donnerlaute des L├╢wen, wenn Parjanya das regenbringende Gew├╢lk macht.

Grassmann

Dem Fuhrmann gleich, der peitschend seine Rosse treibt, l├дsst er erscheinen seine Regenboten schon; Des L├╢wen Donner t├╢nen aus der Ferne her, sobald Pardschanja seine Wolken regnen l├дsst.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe winds blow strong, the lightnings flash, the plural nts spring up, the firmament dissolves; earth becomes (fit) for all creatures when Parjanya fertilizes the soil with showers.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The winds blow forth; the lightning bolts fly. The plants shoot up; the sun swells.
Refreshment arises for all creation, when Parjanya aids the earth with his semen.

Griffith

Forth burst the winds, down come the lightning-flashes: the plants shoot up, the realm of light is streaming.
Food springs abundant for all living creatures, what time Parjanya quickens earth with moisture.

Macdonell

The winds blow forth; to earth the quivering lightnings fall, The plants shoot up; with moisture streams the realm of light. For all the world abundant nourishment is born, When by Parjanya Earth is fertilized with seed.

Geldner

Die Winde wehen los, Blitze fallen, die Pflanzen richten sich auf, die Sonne quillt ├╝ber. Jedwedem Wesen wird Erquickung, wenn Parjanya mit seinem Samen der Erde aufhilft.

Grassmann

Die Winde wehen, Blitze fliegen vor ihm her; die Kr├дuter richten sich empor, der Himmel str├╢mt, Und jedem Wesen wird der Labetrunk erzeugt, sobald Pardschanja mit Erguss die Erd’ erquickt.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬDo you, Parjanya, through whose function the earth is bowed down; through whose function hoofed cattle thrive; through whose function plural nts assume all kinds of forms, grant us great felicity.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

At whose commandment the earth bobs up and down, at whose commandment the hoofed (livestock) quivers,
at whose commandment the plants take on all formsтАФyou, ParjanyaтАФ extend to us great shelter.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Note the unusual geminate in n├бnnam─лti, dissimilated from *n├бmnam─лti.

In p─Бda b the question is whether the scene is set during the thunderstorm, with frightened quivering livestock, or afterwards, as they gambol in new growth.

P─Бda a speaks for the former, c for the latter. Geldner (and, it seems, Witzel Got┼Н) opt for the latter, while I favor the former, though without strong grounds.

The first three p─Бdas of this vs. begin with y├бsya; the fourth does not, but ends with a close phonological match, yacha.

Griffith

Thou at whose bidding earth bows low before thee, at whose command hoofed cattle fly in terror,
At whose behest the plants assume all colours, even thou Parjanya, yield us great protection.

Macdonell

O thou at whose behest the earth bows downward, O thou at whose behest hoofed creatures quiver, At whose behest by plants all shapes are taken: As such, Parjanya, grant to us strong shelter.

Geldner

Bei dessen Walten die Erde sich neigt, bei dessen Walten alles, was Hufe hat, h├╝pft, bei dessen Walten die bunten Pflanzen sprie├Яen, du Parjanya, gew├дhre uns deinen gro├Яen Schutz!

Grassmann

Bei dessen Werk die Erde tief sich neiget, bei dessen Werk sich reget das Behufte, Bei dessen Werk die Kr├дuter bunt sich schm├╝cken, du, o Pardschanja, reiche grossen Schutz uns.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬSend down for us, Maruts, the rain from heaven; drops of the rainy charger descend; come down Parjanya, sprinkling water by this thundering (cloud); you who are the sender of rain, our protector.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Drops of the rainy charger: vс╣Ыс╣гс╣Зo a┼Ыvasya: a┼Ыvasya = vy─Бpakasya, or the pervading rain

Jamison Brereton

Grant us rain from heaven, o Maruts; make the streams of the bullish stallion swell forth.
(Parjanya,) come nearby with this thundering, pouring down the waters as the lord, our father.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The default referent of ├бsuraс╕е pit─Б╠Бnaс╕е тАЬthe lord, our fatherтАЭ here is of course Parjanya, since this is a Parjanya hymn and the subject is urged to pour out water (cf., e.g., Hale, Asura, 46-47). However, I wonder if this is not rather a reference to Dyaus Pitar, or at least an identification of Parjanya with Dyaus Pitar.

For Heaven as pit├бr- ├бsura-, see X.124.3 as well as disc. and other related passages in my тАЬThe Divine Revolution of RV X.124тАЭ (Ged. Staal, 2016), 294, and of course Zeus famously тАШrainsтАЩ in Greek.

Griffith

Send down for us the rain of heaven, ye Maruts, and let the Stallion’s flood descend in torrents.
Come hither with this thunder while thou pourest the waters down, our heavenly Lord and Father.

Macdonell

The rain of heaven bestow, O Maruts, on us, Of your strong steed pour forth the streams abundant. With this thy thundering roar do thou come hither, And shed the waters as our heavenly father.

Geldner

Ihr Marut, spendet uns des Himmels Regen, lasset des Hengstes Strahlen hervorquellen. Komm n├дher mit diesem Gedonnere, die Wasser herabgie├Яend, unser Vater Asura!

Grassmann

Des Himmels Regen spendet uns, o Maruts, des br├╝nst’gen Hengstes Str├╢me lasset schnellen; Komm nah herbei mit dieser Donnerwolke, ergiessend Wasser, uns ein th├дt’ger Vater.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬRaise on high the mighty sheath (of rain), pour down (its contents); let the rivers flow unimpeded to the east; saturate with water both heaven and earth, and let there be abundant beverage for the kine.тАЭ

The great bucketтАФturn it up, pour it down. Let the brooks, unleashed, flow forward.
Inundate Heaven and Earth with ghee. Let there be a good watering hole for the prized cows.

Saturate both the earth and heaven with fatness, and for the cows let there be drink abundant.

рдорд╛рдирд╕рддрд░рдЩреНрдЧрд┐рдгреАрдХреГрддреН

When you, 0 parjanya, roaring,
thundering, kill the evildoers,
to this all jubilate
and whatever exists on earth.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhen, Parjanya, sounding loud and thundering, you destroy the wicked (clouds), this whole (world) rejoices, and all that is upon the earth.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Destroy the wicked clouds: haс╣Гsi duс╣гkс╣Ыtaс╕е, the wicked, i.e. the clouds not yielding their water

Jamison Brereton

When, o Parjanya, constantly roaring, thundering you smash those who do ill,
all of this here, whatever is on the earth, rejoices in response.

Griffith

When thou, with thunder and with roar, Parjanya, smitest sinners down,
This universe exults thereat, yea, all that is upon the earth.

Macdonell

When, O Parjanya, roaring loud, Thou slay’st with thunder wicked men, This universe rejoices then, And everything that is on earth.

Geldner

Wenn du, Parjanya, br├╝llend, donnernd die B├╢sewichter erschl├дgst, so jubelt dir alles, was da auf Erden ist, zu.

Grassmann

Wenn, o Pardschanja, br├╝llend du und donnernd schl├дgst der Frevler Schar, so freut sich diese ganze Welt und alles, was auf Erden ist.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬYou have rained; now check well the rain; you have made the deserts capable of being crossed; you have given birth to plural ns for (man’s) enjoyment; verily you have obtained laudation from the people.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

You have rained rain: (now) hold it back. You have made the
wastelands able to be traversed.
You have begotten the plants for nourishment, and you have found
(this?) inspired thought for the creatures.

Griffith

Thou hast poured down the rain-flood now withhold it. Thou hast made desert places fit for travel.
Thou hast made herbs to grow for our enjoyment: yea, thou hast won thee praise from living creatures.

Macdonell

Thou hast shed rain; pray now withhold it wholly; Thou hast made passable all desert places. To serve as food thou hast made plants to flourish: And hast received the gratitude of creatures.

Grassmann

Elizarenkova

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░рдГ ред рдпрдерд╛ рдЬрдЧрджреАрд╢реНрд╡рд░реЛ рд╡рд░реНрд╖рд╛рднреНрдпрдГ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рд╣рд┐рддрдВ рдЬрдирдпрддрд┐ рддрдереИрд╡ рдзрд╛рд░реНрдорд┐рдХреЛ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рднреНрдпрдГ рд╕реБрдЦрдордзреНрдпрд╛рдкрдХрд╢реНрдЪ рдкреНрд░рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдВ рдЬрдирдпреЗрджрд┐рддрд┐ реерезрежрее рдЕрддреНрд░ рдкрд░реНрдЬрдиреНрдпрд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рджреНрдЧреБрдгрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡реЗрджреНрдпрд╛ рее рдЗрддрд┐ рддреНрд░реНрдпрд╢реАрддрд┐рддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдорд╖реНрдЯрд╛рд╡рд┐рдВрд╢реЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдпрд╛ рдордВрддреНрд░рд╛рдд рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдВрдХрд╛рд░ рдЖрд╣реЗ. рдЬрд╕рд╛ рдЬрдЧрджреАрд╢реНрд╡рд░ рд╡реГрд╖реНрдЯреАрдиреЗ рдкреНрд░рдЬреЗрдЪреЗ рд╣рд┐рдд рдХрд░рддреЛ рддрд╕реЗ рдзрд╛рд░реНрдорд┐рдХ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛рдиреЗ рдкреНрд░рдЬреЗрд▓рд╛ рд╕реБрдЦ рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡реЗ рд╡ рдЕрдзреНрдпрд╛рдкрдХрд╛рдиреЗ рдмреБрджреНрдзреА рдЙрддреНрдкрдиреНрди рдХрд░рд╛рд╡реА. рее резреж рее
